Shen Bao Literary Weekly

Tentative Explanation of "A Midsummer Night's Dream" 159

— Fang Turen

Shakespeare's most famous comedy "A Midsummer Night's Dream" is currently being shown in Shanghai, which is a cause for celebration. As the translator of the original play, having left the Cathay Theater, it is my duty to offer an explanation of the real feelings I obtained from wandering through the dream of the English poetic saint of over three hundred years ago.

How does the poet create his dream? Look at this:

"The poet's eye, in a fine frenzy rolling,

Doth glance from heaven to earth, from earth to heaven;

And as imagination bodies forth

The forms of things unknown, the poet's pen

Turns them to shapes and gives to airy nothing

A local habitation and a name."

—Act V, Scene 1

After reading this great poet's confession about the method of creation, it is easy to know that there is a reason why this "A Midsummer Night's Dream," which is interwoven by three main threads, is so moving. The poet does not build his dream in the air; he has his bricks and tiles. Plutarch's "Life of Theseus," Ovid's "Metamorphoses" (Book IV, about the legend of Thisbe and Pyramus), and the legends about little fairies circulating in the poet's hometown of Warwick are all the bricks and tiles the poet used when creating his dream. Is this plagiarism? Absolutely not! The poet is "turning them to shapes." The humble poet even uses the closing remarks of the original play to express his creative attitude:

"If we shadows have offended,

Think but this, and all is mended,

That you have but slumber'd here

While these visions did appear.

And this weak and idle theme,

No more yielding but a dream,

Gentles, do not reprehend:

If you pardon, we will mend:

And, as I am an honest Puck,

If we have unearned luck

Now to 'scape the serpent's tongue,

We will make amends ere long;

Else the Puck a liar call.

So, good night unto you all.

Give me your hands, if we be friends,

And Robin shall restore amends."

The concrete method of creation and the very honest creative attitude used by the poet in this "A Midsummer Night's Dream" are both worth learning from.

What exactly did the poet dream in this "A Midsummer Night's Dream"? The dream is built in Athens, and the era is the mythological era of ancient Greece: The poet's dream must not be a dream of reality. This kind of argument is ridiculous. Shakespeare, who is revered as a realist poet, even in this "A Midsummer Night's Dream," dreams of the most realistic things. Even the Poet Laureate John Masefield, when commenting on "A Midsummer Night's Dream," had to admit that "Shakespeare grasped all the power of the English spirit. He made a large picture of English characters." The Duke of Athens portrayed by Shakespeare is the epitome of the 17th-century English aristocracy; the Athenian craftsmen are the epitome of the 17th-century English rural laborers; and the mischievous little fairies are also the realistic characters in the minds of the English country folk. Although "A Midsummer Night's Dream" is draped in Athenian clothes, the flesh inside the clothes is completely English. This is the reason why Shakespeare is revered as a realist poet.

Who will the poet present this "A Midsummer Night's Dream" to? Regardless of the year it was written, this "A Midsummer Night's Dream" was written to celebrate a wedding—or for a private performance in a wealthy family, or perhaps for a performance in the court. Although this cannot be determined, this play must have been presented at a court wedding. However, to conclude that Shakespeare was a despicable court poet, "a parasite, living on the generosity of his feudal superiors with an unashamed face," is also a mechanical assertion. In "A Midsummer Night's Dream," which is based on the Athenian craftsmen pleasing the Athenian monarchs, the poet is explaining his progressive worldview to his audience. The Athenian craftsmen's crude, simple, and sincere nature, without any malice, combines with the more poetic mood of the upper class like brothers, so that the audience will naturally feel a kind of attraction that treats all mankind equally. The simplicity of the lower class and the open-mindedness of the upper class are smoothly blended into one.

Disguised Appearance and Convenient Transformation 160

— Qin Wen

In order to make it easier for readers to be moved, when writing novels, people often describe other people's stories as if they had experienced them themselves; because readers generally have a considerable understanding and belief in the author, they are more likely to sympathize when told that it is the author's own story; moreover, in "autobiographical" form, the tone is often direct, making it easier to understand.

Sometimes, however, one's own story is written as someone else's, because there are things that conflict with laws and morals, and if they were stated directly, they would not be tolerated by public opinion; or it may be necessary to keep secrets and not disclose them publicly. Only by being in the position of a third party and writing in "biographical" form (or third-person form) can one express oneself freely and happily.

Changing things like this is a means of "convenient transformation"; although the form is changed, "authenticity" can still be maintained. An autobiography is different from a "self-narrative"; a self-narrative can also be written in biographical form. In literature, convenient transformation is a common technique, and those who know it can see it at a glance.

In literary works, there are even more drastic changes in things; according to the theory that "literature is a symbol of depression," this is "disguised appearance."

There are probably two reasons for disguised appearance: first, because it is not possible to express directly, one has to make use of the topic; for example, one secretly falls in love with a member of the opposite sex, admiring them very urgently, but is hindered by ethical customs, and it is not possible to be together in reality; "reason" dares not think about it anymore, but "emotion" refuses to give up, and still deeply regrets, forming a "ball of depression," wanting to move at all times, and taking any opportunity to erase its original form, entrusting it to relevant facts to vent.

Second, one has deep depression, but it is somewhat inexplicable, because it is fundamental, unfamiliar, and also abstract; to vent, one has to find concrete facts to express it; like being bitten by a poisonous snake in a dream, or being beaten by someone, and still feeling pain after waking up, and even developing sores at the wound and producing pus. The place where the sores develop was already poisoned and had hidden pain, but it was not felt during the busy day; the "subconscious" felt it, so it took the opportunity to borrow the existing concepts of snake bites and beatings as a concrete report; this kind of disguised appearance is very common in literature.

Whether it is convenient transformation or disguised appearance, the result is a kind of "symbolism"; although the head and face are changed, it is still an analogy and representation of the original body. Convenient transformation and disguised appearance have similar functions, but they are fundamentally different: convenient transformation is due to the author's intention and is a kind of "technique"; disguised appearance is due to the unconscious and is something that cannot be sought. Probably, the result of convenient transformation is only "broad symbolism"; the result of disguised appearance is "narrow symbolism," which is what is called true symbolism in literature.

In "pure literature," narrow symbolism holds a higher position; however, "the literature of life" is more objective and emphasizes reason, so it is more important to use convenient transformation, because this can be done by force, while disguised appearance is difficult to grasp.

Although it cannot be sought, disguised appearance is one of the essential qualities of literature. The literature of life focuses on exploring problems, but it must use the essential qualities of literature to easily move the reader; otherwise, it is only theory and does not count as literature. The so-called cannot be sought does not mean that it is absolutely impossible to do, but that it comes slowly. Authors of the literature of life, to make use of disguised appearance, must first have proper theory as a prerequisite and temper their personality, then the result of disguised appearance will have a great atmosphere;—aiming at great undertakings at all times, the things borrowed by disguised appearance will naturally also be great. Otherwise, leaving it to nature, emotion is originally blind, and the result of "unconscious suggestion" is inevitably just "flowers" and "moons." Although the "flowers" and "moons" in general literary works are sometimes also due to disguised appearance, what do they mean?

Invoking the Gods 161

— Ouyang Shan

It was a beautiful summer morning in 1928. Hei Gu Li Ju, who specialized in the human trafficking business, ran from Furongwei, a neighboring village, to Changba. He walked along the narrow paths, sometimes climbing up hills, sometimes hiding at the foot of mountains, as if he were a small boat gliding on waves.

At this time, Changba had just gone through "village cleansing" – a kind of open robbery and massacre. The residents had only returned from outside the village two days before to tidy up their furniture and bury the dead. Charred woodenware and clothes were discarded everywhere. A pungent, fishy stench permeated the ravaged hills and the burned and chopped forests. White smoke from still unextinguished fires rose from the distant and nearby slopes. Besides the waste and garbage, piles of dried or fresh tree bark lay everywhere. Whenever Hei Gu Li Ju passed such a place, he paid attention to whether there were any exposed corpses and pinched his nose with his fingers. In this "village cleansing," the village head Xu Dacheng was killed. … The residents had nothing to eat, so they gathered wild rattan vegetables and field herbs, mixed them with bitter lotus seeds and wild asparagus, and burned them to eat. As a result, all the villagers suffered from severe diarrhea.

On the eastward-facing hillside beside the Ke family, Ke Di was kneeling next to the earthen wall, invoking the gods.

"Great Emperor Ziwei, you know everything, but I'll say it anyway, the same as last night and this morning: give us something to eat! Great Emperor Ziwei, you know everything…"

She prayed devoutly in a low voice, repeating herself. She was very thin and wore ragged, all-black coarse cloth clothes. Her braid coiled on her back like a small snake, and her whole body was huddled together. The earthen wall, almost collapsing, stood precariously beside her, threatening to fall and bury her completely at any moment. At that time, she was only twelve years old.

Hei Gu Li Ju and her father, Ke Laosi, were arguing fiercely in front of the sickbed. Because he was asking for too high a price, Li Ju mocked him. Ke Di had never seen her father so angry or so insulted before. Her mother sat on a hoe, wailing uncontrollably.

"Ke Laosi, you're completely ignorant of the market price! Children are given away at times like these! If someone wants her, you should know that the child will live a few days longer than with you, and maybe even grow up. You should be thanking people. If you're dreaming, let me wake you up: good children are worth ten dollars per year of age, five dollars per year of age! Just keep yelling!"

"A child can only be sold once, you idiot!" Ke Laosi scolded him. "I'm selling a person now. Once she leaves the door, she'll never come back."

"Anyone who comes to me, Li Ju, is selling people… If they leave the door and keep coming back, that's called dealing with the in-laws! I've never been a matchmaker."

"Have a conscience, you dead dog! A human heart is made of flesh."

"Then I'm sorry…"

"Don't go!"

Ke Laosi loudly stopped him, and then said to him:

"Okay, you know very well that I have no choice but to sell! Now you can say whatever you want, but after I get better, be careful that my axe doesn't chop your neck!…"

"Then what about me? Am I supposed to chop up your corpse with my axe?"

Ke Di, frightened, quietly slipped out the door. In front of the chicken coop, she knelt down again and continued her prayer.

"Great Emperor Ziwei, you know everything…"

It was very quiet in the mountains. The sparse sounds of axes chopping trees and the heavy echoes of piles being driven into the hard earth did not disturb anything. Sunlight flooded the uneven and hazy village like golden lake water. When the Ke family was at its most prosperous, they had raised four mottled chicks in the chicken coop. Now, only a few short bamboo branches stuck diagonally in the black soil remained there.

Ke Di temporarily stopped her prayer and, together with Hei Gu Li Ju, left her chicken coop forever and ran to the world beyond the mountains.

Nostalgic Song 162

— Ren Jun

Five or six years ago – my hometown was originally a poor village; but, thank God! Everyone still managed to live in an atmosphere of peace: putting down their hoes, people could still afford half a tael of liquor, and every year there were still one or two joyous god-welcoming festivals; young people never forgot to sing folk songs, and old men loved to have a hint of a smile on their faces.

Just last year or the year before – although the drought brought starvation and freezing, and war brought sighs and tears, the present sorrow had already chased away the past joy; but it was still considered a human world: you could still hear dogs barking, and you could still hear chickens crowing.

But this year – the Yellow River's turbid waves are just like a gluttonous poisonous dragon! It swallowed our thatched huts, swallowed our fields, and even swallowed our livestock and children…

At this moment, the water has finally receded, but our home is just a wasteland! In the wasteland – there are only a few skinny dogs that weren't drowned, searching everywhere for their old homes; countless crows are fighting over carrion, cawing in the setting sun…

Passing Through the Strait of Malacca 163

— Fei Er

I borrowed a sampan from a friend, and a familiar companion took me out to sea. Leaving Zhongjie, passing "Lao Ba Sai," the sea came into view. Months of noise and a gray and melancholy life were about to come to an end. When the sampan approached the "Jida" steamer, the companion said:

"Come back from Penang soon! Zhongjie has lively cafes."

I nodded and smiled, wondering when I would return to Singapore. If there's food to eat and work to do, everywhere is home! Otherwise, I will come back to Zhongjie. Zhongjie has my friends, Zhongjie's exit has the sea, Zhongjie's coffee shops have all kinds of people, and Zhongjie has food!

The ship set sail under the blazing sun. It rounded a corner of Lion Island, leaving behind the bustling and crowded docks and warehouses. The flag of Penang Hill looked small, and the road disappeared at the corner of the island. Red sand was exposed in the small hills on the shore, and the bare hills did not have black stones. The ship slowly passed between two low, small red hills, and the waves hit the coast of Lion Island in the distance.

On the ship, I ran into a shipmate who was a relative. He said:

"Penang isn't better than Singapore. There are unemployed people everywhere; miners from Ipoh and Perak leave the country from here all the time. This 'garden of the South' is desolate now."

I said:

"Even if the flower is withered, one must still take a look. Perhaps there are still flowers of hope in the withered flower clusters."

The next day, we passed through the Strait of Malacca. The wind was calm and the waves were gentle in this narrow strait, and the ripples in the sea were like the wind blowing across a pond. Occasionally there were seagulls, and occasionally there were sailboats. Besides that, the sea reflected golden light under the intense sun, and the fishing boats of the fishermen were invisible in the distance.

At about three o'clock in the afternoon, I saw a fishing boat passing through the lonely sea. It was lonely, with its sails fully raised, and the hull was blackened by tar. In the bow, it looked like a leaf in the distance, and then, in the original appearance of a sailboat, it floated lonely past the stern.

My relative, who was a clerk on the ship, told me:

"This must be a fugitive, habitually crossing the waves between Malaya and Sumatra. Fishermen's boats can't travel so far, and they don't go as leisurely as a lame immortal crossing the sea! Look at how the boat sways! It looks just like a lame duck."

I didn't say anything. I wondered why there were no sea roars or raging waves in the Strait of Malacca. A calm and gentle sea is not the norm; I don't want to see a calm ocean!

In the evening, the ship arrived at Penang between rows of beautiful mountains. Years of longing had been fulfilled, and after seeing the lush tropical green mountains, the Strait of Malacca was lightly let go.

Miscellaneous Memories of Fleeing (Continued) 164

— Liu Ming

Perhaps they were packing things for the escape at home? In short, I didn't succeed in peeking. My mother and aunts were, of course, extremely disheartened. But I was overjoyed. I first ate a lot of peanuts that were lying on the ground unattended, and when I came back, my two small pockets were almost bursting.

During these three or four days of fleeing, the adults must have had a real scare, right? That was when they saw a dozen or twenty fellows with sheep horns, red-tasseled spears, and broadswords passing outside the door. Everyone immediately hid in the latrine, and told me not to stick my head out from the straw to look around. After a while, they heard that those people were going to help the Tongzhi Society, and they immediately laughed and scolded as they crawled out. At that time, I thought, isn't this as fun as the hide-and-seek game we kids play?

Later, when we went back, whenever I remembered these interesting things, I would always tug at my mother's sleeve and ask...

"Mom, when? When will we have to flee again?"

My mother, who understood the suffering of fleeing, puffed out her cheeks and scolded:

"What, you're asking for bad luck! ...Don't ask about such things!"

Later, I also fled many times outside, but the situation was like eating Western pills. The sugar coating on the outside had already melted away, and all that was left was the bitter and spicy taste.

New Residence 165

— Wang Renshu

It has been less than a month since I moved into this new residence, and already friends have been advising me to move. But I always watch as car after car drives up to other people's doors for their moves, while I delay day after day. My friends' intentions are appreciated. However, how could they know that I have other ideas?

I do not love this new residence. The so-called new residence is only two cramped floors, barely enough to hold my knees, and there are absolutely no conditions that ordinary people would find desirable. However, if I really had to move away, I could not help but feel some reluctance.

This new residence is on East Sports Association Road, near the shooting range. But when I first moved in, I didn't know that. After I had settled down a bit and was sitting by the window reading a book, a series of "pipi-papai" sounds frightened me. I turned around and looked out the window, and then I discovered that the sound was coming from a dark green earthen hill. On the earthen hill was a row of ochre-colored walls, and under the walls were a few black wooden plaques with white characters! Arabic numerals! and the pieces of white paper that were pasted on the plaques rose and fell with the sound of the gunshots from time to time. All of this was vividly displayed before my eyes. Only then did I suddenly realize that I was actually living at the foot of the shooting range.

Who wouldn't shudder! Perhaps everyone would think that as a people of the colony, I should be afraid of being treated as a ochre-colored wall, a black wooden plaque, or a piece of white paper on this dark green earthen hill! However, I immediately felt that this new residence was suitable for me. Living as a person of the twentieth century, how can one not be accustomed to hearing this most inspiring and greatest of music! The sound of shooting at this range is truly otherworldly, the most arrogant and wonderful music that cannot be found anywhere else in the world!

There was also a time when I listened quietly to the music inside modern Western-style buildings. This situation was exactly as the Japanese writer Kazuo Uchimura wrote in his novel Leprosy!

"His room, number 65 on the second floor, was located slightly towards the center of the long corridor... All the sounds that arose in this corner of the building seemed to naturally converge towards the center. Although the interior was completely divided, in one corner of this large box-like building, any sound would cause a faint echo in the four walls. The echo flowed towards the center and gradually faded away. - The sound of men's straw sandals passing through the corridor; the quiet voices of two or three people secretly avoiding prying eyes; the grinding sound of transport carts; the sound of meal boxes being thrown down three times a day; the heavy footsteps of the guards and the clanging of their swords. - …These mixed sounds, once they flowed here, became a kind of harmonious melody. This is a world where people are strictly forbidden to speak to their companions, and from morning to night, one can only see gray walls and the blue sky through iron-barred windows, but even in this, there is still a naturally brewing world of music, bringing such a complex timbre…"

This state of mind is probably shared by modern young people who have quietly spent some time in Western-style buildings! However, this is the most wonderful music of modern times, with a quiet timbre. Compared to the music I hear in my ears at this moment, it is quite the "opposite".

Those sounds initially came in sparse clusters. The tone was short and well-rounded. It was as if a group of wild children, in a forest where the leaves were yellow and falling, had picked up some chestnuts and thrown them into the fire, causing "pong" or "peng" explosions, followed by "whala!" consonants. I felt a kind of valley tranquility. Afterwards, the sound was continuous. It was like accumulated snow pressing on bamboo, a strong wind shaking violently, and the bamboo stems bursting, "pong la! Pong la! Pong la!" A series of sounds reverberated through the clouds. I felt the sounds of the white snow and the sense of the song being too high for many to appreciate. Then, perhaps, there would be silence, and the sigh of the wind would flow through the still air. Perhaps there would be an even more激厉, clearer, and more passionate sound, like celebrating the New Year, the sound of firecrackers like a happy and peaceful atmosphere. And this is the voices of people around, the sound of wheels, the cries of vendors, the sound of horses' hooves, the cries of children, the whistle of trains, the rustling of grass tips, the rustling of fallen leaves, and the orderly footsteps of foreign soldiers on the cinder road! All of this is suppressed low, fragile and dim, desolate and bleak, but it becomes the only consonant of this great and powerful ensemble. Therefore, if the former music is said to have a quiet timbre, then this music can be said to have a dynamic timbre. The former music is often loved by pale-faced people close to death; while this music is loved by young people who are full of energy and should be restrained from fighting. Listening to the former music can make people fall into a deep sleep, gradually becoming silent and entering the state of Nirvana. But listening to this music will inevitably make people's blood splash, wanting to dye the whole world red! I have to be in this new residence, listening to this most great and wonderful music in the world, which deeply makes me reflect on the destiny of mankind from time to time. I truly want to thank this ancient land with tears streaming down my face, and how can I bear to move away from it even for a moment!

Secondly, according to my lifestyle habits, I always move my body a little every morning when I wake up. After arriving here, I walk along East Sports Association Road. The next morning, I strolled to a large bridge. Oh! Under the veil-like morning mist, what a beautiful and quiet residence there was! It was surrounded by bamboo fences, and the bamboo fences were covered with lush green vines. In the middle were four or five barracks-style plank houses. The millet-colored planks were all hidden among the verdant and luxuriant branches and leaves of vines, willows, and peach trees, like the secluded scene in Du Fu's poem "Beautiful Woman" where she "leads vines to mend the thatched hut". Outside the bamboo fence, the fields were divided into small plots, planted with vegetables, chrysanthemums, peach trees, willows, and the like, sparsely and densely, left to nature as if no human labor had been added. In the middle was a round patch of ground paved with broken tiles, surrounded by saplings of cypresses as thick as an arm. At this time, the sun had not yet risen, but the desolate mist was gradually receding. The crowing of chickens in the small house, and the barking of dogs in the neighboring house, proudly sang together, creating a scene where even chickens and dogs could become immortals. After a while, a Chinese compatriot, wearing short clothes and barefoot, carried a square wooden table out of the small house and placed it on the altar made of broken tiles. He stood there in a daze for a while, then turned around and went back in, and carried out two brown rattan chairs. Each chair had a brown soft cushion. He arranged the rattan chairs opposite each other. He diligently wiped them for a while, and then stood there in a daze again before slowly walking in. His actions were full of the leisurely and idyllic charm of the medieval pastoral era, which was perfectly matched with this lazy and slow melody. After he went in, a man in a Western suit came out wearing slippers. After walking a short distance, he used his left hand to cover his forehead and looked up at the sky. The sky was full of white clouds! Then he raised the newspaper in his right hand and looked at it. Slowly and methodically, he walked to the earthen altar and plopped down on the rattan chair, slowly yawning, put the newspaper on the table, stretched his fists a few times, yawned again, and then sat down and leaned on the table to read the newspaper. When the sun spat out a touch of pale light, and the sound of chickens and dogs gradually became sparse, a woman in ancient costume, wearing a white apron, came out gracefully holding a delicate tea tray. She placed the teapot from the tray in front of the man, and said something softly as if, and then sat down opposite him. She poured a cup of tea for the man, and then poured a cup for herself, picked up a newspaper, and read it quietly. This middle-aged couple was quietly in the silent language of nature in the morning. - This couldn't help but make me imagine things from before the Three Dynasties. However, compared to Tao Yuanming's Peach Blossom Spring, it must be "more than equal to" it! Although the world has already advanced to the twentieth century, such a medieval pastoral flavor and leisurely sentiment is also a dog grabbing a carpet, a barbarous legacy that we, the so-called inferior nation in the world, envy!

The kindness of my friends who advise me to move is appreciated! But I am a person of the twentieth century, and I must develop the habit of loving to listen to the great music of the end of this century! I can't bear to give up my new residence even for a moment!

Reviewing the Old to Know the New? 166

(2) December 25th is the anniversary of the Yunnan Uprising. The cotton yarn exchange will be temporarily closed on that day for one day. All trading of this month's cotton yarn futures will cease on the 24th. Please take note.

Yesterday, American cotton opened with fluctuating market conditions due to uncertainty in the silver market, unpredictable European political situations, and delays in the Supreme Court's rulings. Price fluctuations ranged from one to four points across different months. Subsequently, long positions were closed and then reopened, with some activity from Far Eastern buyers. However, due to falling silver prices and reduced demand from the industry, prices fell slightly. Mid-session, short covering and local buying provided some rebound. Finally, large-scale long position liquidations and heavy selling led to a weak market. As a result, spot prices fell by 30 points, and futures prices fell by 25 to 31 points. English cotton spot prices rose by two points, and futures rose by one point. The futures initially rose due to short covering, but then weakened due to long liquidations. Calculated in terms of local currency, Pungole rose by 1.5 to 1.75 rupees, Oomra rose by 1.5 rupees, and Broach rose by 1.375 rupees. Original telegram records are on the left. (Telegram dated 11th)

Grains: Flour Market Heavily Hit 175

Yesterday, the flour market showed a further decline across all months. Opening prices in the morning were initially based on foreign wheat quotations, with Chicago down two to three cents and Canada down eight tenths to one cent. Market sentiment was unsteady due to the decline in foreign wheat and significant fluctuations in the foreign silver market. Opening prices immediately fell by one or two cents. Trading was active in subsequent sessions, with prices fluctuating. However, at the afternoon opening, the market was initially stable, but then the closure of the Xinda Flour Mill (Xingji leased the Lida factory site and operated as a single entity) caused concern. Although there was no direct relationship with the exchange, customers with hedged positions were potentially affected. In addition, the small rebound in gold prices further softened sentiment, leading to widespread abandonment of hedging, which intensified the decline in nearby months. Nearby months fell by eight or nine cents, and distant months fell by five or six cents. Looking ahead, if customers do not take delivery this month, there may be further declines.

Wheat Futures See Selling Pressure in Every Session 176

Yesterday, the wheat futures market was initially stable in the morning session, but sentiment was weak due to falling foreign wheat quotations. Prices for all months fell by three or four cents. In the afternoon session, the market suddenly experienced a sharp decline due to the significant implications of the silver issue, which inevitably affected the prices of various commodities. Moreover, rumors of 680 hedged positions in the flour market triggered a sharp decline. As a result, long positions became weaker, leading to selling pressure in every session and a sharp drop in prices. Although inventories are not abundant, sales are sluggish amid the current economic difficulties, which exert significant pressure on the market, resulting in a sharp decline. Both nearby and distant months fell by more than ten cents, serving as a warning to speculators. The spot wheat market is weak due to poor mill demand, and asking prices have fallen by another two or three cents. Shandong wheat is quoted at 4.80 yuan, Suzhou/Lai wheat at 4.78 yuan, Jiangbei wheat at 4.77 yuan, and Chuzhou wheat at 4.76 yuan. It is said that Fuxin handled 3,000 bags.

Rice from Hexia Sells Well to Northern Merchants 177

(South Shanghai) Yesterday, a total of over fifty dealers arrived with supplies (over ten thousand shih of goods). Sales in this district continued to be active due to overcast weather. Tianjin and Qingdao merchants also handled over three thousand bags, leading to a slight tightening of the market. High-quality Booda rice was stable, and intermediate-quality goods were scarce, fetching five cents more. Sutong glutinous rice also fetched a few cents to about ten cents more. Early rice saw no changes. Duyang sharp rice and Yinbianyuan rice were all stable.

(North Shanghai) Yesterday, supplies from various sources in Hexia remained abundant, with about sixty dealers arriving. Demand for white glutinous rice at stores was even weaker than yesterday. Wholesale transactions were slow, and prices fell slightly by about ten cents. Early rice followed suit, falling by nearly ten cents. Booda rice sales were stagnant, and liquor merchants were quiet, with prices falling slightly by about ten cents. Yangbu sharp rice continued to sell, and prices were stable. Transactions of customer sharp rice were few. All other goods showed signs of weakness.

While Arrivals of Customer Xian Rice Are Not Strong 178

Yesterday, the customer Xian rice market saw arrivals from various sources, but the quantities were not as high as in previous days. Only over two thousand bags of new rice arrived, mainly from Jiangxi and Wenzhou/Taizhou. As arrivals decreased, sales in this district did not stagnate, and the market stabilized. The daily outflow included 2,461 bags of Jiangxi rice, 1,200 bags of Wenzhou/Taizhou rice, 189 bags of Hunan rice, and 200 bags of Siamese Yangyuan rice, all handled by this district. There is hope for a market recovery; otherwise, with the end of the year approaching and economic conditions tightening, arrivals will inevitably increase, leading to desperate selling and making it difficult for the market to sustain.

6,000 Bags of Sesame and Raw Goods Sold; No Significant Changes in Soybeans 179

Yesterday, the spot price of raw sesame remained at 11.8 yuan due to the difficulty in raising the market price of clean goods at foreign firms. Transactions were limited to only two to three hundred tons. Therefore, the sentiment of cargo owners shifted, leading to transactions involving combined deliveries of stocked goods. Total transactions for various sesame seeds in the city amounted to 6,000 bags. Market trends were initially weak and then stabilized, but the overall trend still depended on the sales of foreign firms.

There were still no significant changes in soybeans. Downward pressure was limited because of high preparation costs and continued interest from manufacturers. Yesterday, 600 bags of Bengbu beans, 600 bags of Luohe green/yellow beans, and 700 bags of Xinyangzhou beans were sold. Arrivals of Zhadou were more abundant, with inquiries from Fuzhou, Ningbo, and local merchants (daily transactions of over 1,000 bags). However, the market sentiment was difficult to stabilize. Doudousha yellow beans maintained a high, stable, and then soft position.

North-South Goods: Xinghua Longan Land Prices Rise; Miscellaneous Returned Goods Loosen 180

Due to poor harvests this year, the highest-grade Zheng Er first batch of Xinghua longan was initially priced at over 110 yuan. Although prices were high and sales were slow, land prices did not ease as a result. Recently, they have risen further, leading to price increases in Shanghai. Yesterday, the highest-grade Zheng Er reached over 120 yuan in the market. However, other miscellaneous longan varieties, with larger inventories, were very accommodating in the market, and outflow was difficult despite efforts to stimulate demand, with prices slightly softening.

Piece Goods: Overcoat Business Suddenly Flourishes; Prices for Men's and Women's Overcoats Are Similar 181

Lately, the woolen overcoat business has been extremely busy for clothing stores. Women's colored overcoat stores in the Fourth Avenue area have been particularly busy because workers have resumed work after the strike. An ordinary Concord women's overcoat generally sells for 65 yuan in national currency, an A-Pang-Sheng overcoat sells for 44 yuan, a Bi-Long collar women's overcoat sells for 33 yuan, a custom-made foreign fox fur overcoat sells for 25-26 yuan, and a ready-made overcoat sells for 19 yuan. A custom-made men's Genuine Old 1005 riding breeches wool-blend overcoat costs 35 foreign yuan per piece, and a new 1005 ready-made overcoat costs 31 yuan. Zhanglan and Japanese riding breeches wool-blend overcoats cost 26-27 yuan. A genuine human-shaped woolen-blend overcoat generally sells for 15-16 yuan, and a second-grade one sells for only 12.5 yuan.

Shen Bao Local Supplement

Talks

Promoting the Aviation Industry 183

— Zhang Ji

Amidst the intense bombing of undefended cities in Abyssinia by Italian aircraft in East Africa and the continuous reconnaissance of the Pingjin region by aircraft from a certain country, we read two more encouraging pieces of news: First, Xu Qixing, a young overseas Chinese, gained admiration from the Dutch people after successfully flying his self-made aircraft to and from Java in the Netherlands. He was subsequently hired by the Dutch to establish a large-scale aircraft manufacturing factory in Java. Mr. Xu also stated that he intends to take a leave of absence next spring to fly his self-made aircraft back to his homeland, hoping to find an opportunity to serve the country. Second, Li Jingzong, the general manager of Eurasia Aviation Corporation, is advocating gliding as a preliminary form of flight training. He is currently seeking support from leaders of the Party and the state to jointly initiate the establishment of a Gliding Research Association in Shanghai, with plans to establish branches in various locations in the future.

We know that the 20th century is the age of flight. Since World War I, countries around the world have been striving to promote the aviation industry. Today, it has not only become the sole weapon in military affairs but also has made significant progress in civil aviation. The successful crossing of the Pacific Ocean by the American "China Clipper" (the significance of which we will not discuss for the moment) is one example. Given China's vast territory and inconvenient transportation, the urgent need to develop civil aviation is undeniable. As for military affairs, the lessons of the January 28th Incident are not only deeply imprinted in the minds of the people of Shanghai but also unforgettable for the people of the entire country. Its need is just as urgent as that of civil aviation.

While the promotion of aviation should be planned comprehensively by the government, the enthusiasm of the people for aviation is particularly important. By aviation enthusiasm, I believe that not only should there be enthusiastic material contributions, but there should also be active training in technical aspects, such as mechanical construction, flight techniques, and air defense knowledge, all of which are very important. Although gliding is a preliminary form of flight training, its meaning is significant. As for Mr. Xu's self-made aircraft, its success in inspiring our enthusiasm for aviation extends beyond just the technical aspects. I hope that these two encouraging pieces of news will promote China's nascent aviation industry.

The Sea of Emotion 184

— Simon

Emotion is a sea, and my body is like a boat floating on it, drifting with the waves, never still. The sea, the majestic sea of emotion, stretches as far as the eye can see, connecting to the endless sky, deep and unfathomable. The changes in the sea are as unpredictable as the changes in the weather. The sea of emotion may have even more rapidly changing forms. Therefore, my body's boat often faces the possibility of being capsized in the sea of emotion.

Suddenly, a storm breaks out, and the waves of the sea surge like hills. The emotional waves of the sea crash against my body's boat, shaking it violently. At this time, I am calm, letting fate decide, because such encounters are always unavoidable, and there is no way to salvage them. I am prepared for the final sinking of my body's boat, forgetting everything at the same time. But in the end, it has never sunk. After enduring several attacks from the wind and waves, my body's boat, although still without leaks or holes, has been worn down into an exceptionally old and dilapidated state.

The movement of the sea of emotion is immeasurable, capable of destroying everything when it roars suddenly, and capable of carrying everything when it calms down. The body's boat carried on the sea of emotion holds my life, as well as some hopes and some aspirations, along with some fears and some tremblings. I am constantly worried that the unprovoked waves of emotion will engulf the boat, but when it remains unchanged for a long time, the boat forgets its worries and sails leisurely and slowly, as if harboring a kind of curiosity for the thrill of encountering danger.

I am just a boat drifting in the heart of the sea of emotion.

Page 16

Separation 185

— Cheng Quan

Friend, after wandering in a distant ancient city for a year, you have now quietly returned, still dragging a listless body and a pair of tired eyes, like a shadow.

After a long separation during which we had no opportunity to exchange letters, you brought a belly full of sights and feelings from afar (how fragmented they are!) to visit me from a great distance. We shook hands, and in an instant, we both felt each other's indescribable hardship and unease. We both fell silent involuntarily, and all the carefully prepared greetings after the separation were snatched away by the terrible black hand of deathly silence.

Who can say anything, who can tell anyone anything pleasant! We have helplessly lost the courage to make perfunctory greetings - what we saw from each other's tired bodies and angry eyes was a pile of fragments of life! We are both capable of explaining each other's lives with our own. Why must we drag out unpleasant, fragmented pieces? - That is useless, that is foolish, that is meddlesome and cruel.

But, silent and silent, I finally said:

"Now, you have finally returned. After living in the ancient city for a year, what is the scenery of the ancient city like? Tell me a little about it."

Blinking his eyes and turning his pale face away, he said softly: "Yes, I have returned. The ancient city is still the same ancient city; but it is no longer our world."

The voice was so calm, so low, so low that it was even difficult to distinguish its words. However, these words, falling gently into our ears, were like a top-violent bomb, with a loud sound like a big thunder, shaking the bottom of people's hearts.

And the buzzing voice continued as calmly as the rocks on a desolate mountain: "The ancient city is no longer our world. It is no longer suitable for our lives, so I came back."

The tone was calm, but this calm tone struck my heart anxiously and violently, like the cold winter night's storm. I trembled: "There will be no place in this world that is ours! There will be no place for us to live everywhere! That is the tragedy of a hard and humiliating era..."

Silence was almost about to occupy the cold space of this small room again. We were both afraid of this man-eating silence! So, my friend began to move his pale and colorless lips and uttered some other words: "And you, how are you living? How are you passing the days? People cannot go back to thinking about the past days - a year has passed."

"Yes, a year has passed," I was at a loss: a year has passed, and how viciously has life punished me in this year? What words shall I use to tell him? Where shall I start? Life is a pile of shattered pieces, and these pieces are so broken and incomplete that they cannot be put back together. What is good for me to say?

However, I finally said: "Alas, life is so bad, it is very much like a poisonous whip that cannot be broken..."

"Stop! Stop! Don't say any more! Don't anymore..."

He shouted like a madman; and, following this shout, we were silent again. An invisible whip danced flexibly on our bodies, circling, waving...

The night fell silently, and the small room was unusually dark. Winter was already deep, and the wind was whistling outside. I seemed to still hear: "It is no longer our world."

My friend stood up, nodded, and dragged his long, thin shadow out wordlessly. I followed him to the door, shook his hand, and then slowly stepped onto the cold street and walked away.

Looking at his back, I said so much: "A year has passed."

Li Sandie 186

— Jing Yun

The sun floated above the treetops to the east, and its scorching rays shone directly through the small window onto the floor, warming Li Sandie's naked belly and waking him up.

Li Sandie prided himself on being an old foreigner, whose habits were just like those of the dark-skinned aborigines. He didn't need to "shower" early in the morning, just as the sun was about to peek out. He often faced the "new foreigners" who had just come from "Tangshan" (China), grinning with his dark teeth, half lecturing and half boasting: "You are new here, you can't be greedy for sleep early in the morning. Before the sun comes out, you have to get up and "shower" - don't be afraid of the cold, pour water straight down from the top of your head, and you won't get sick, you won't be unacclimatized. - You are not like me, I have even warmed up the ground! Haha, new customers"!

He jumped up in one go, walked down the dirt steps, and used his two palms as gourds to scoop water from the water barrel and splash it on his face, considering it his face wash. Then, he pulled out a five-cent "Style Dan" (Siamese currency) from his waistband, bought a pack of bamboo leaf rice from the aborigine squatting at the door, and ate it as breakfast. After that, he picked up his bamboo pole and walked out of the low, dilapidated fence gate.

Not far from the fence gate was an earthen slope, on which stood many tall palm trees with dense, lush green leaves. Beneath them was a low, thatched-roof hut, which was the Xing Lao Er's wine shop. Although the signboard was so mottled that the words on it could not be recognized, everyone who lived here knew about "Xing Ji Wine Shop," the oldest wine shop there!

Li Sandie looked at Xing Ji Wine Shop and felt his throat itching a little. He thought to himself, how flavorful it would be to have half a jin of white spirits to drink. It felt as if his strength would increase after drinking the wine. But as soon as he thought of how Xing's boss had been pressing him hard for the considerable amount of his overdue wine bill, his heart felt as cold as if it had been doused with cold water.

"What's there to be afraid of? The wine bill has to be paid anyway - what does it matter if I owe a little more"! Li Sandie's desire for wine had already surged, and muttering to himself, his feet involuntarily turned to the entrance of Xing Ji Wine Shop.

The plump Xing boss was standing at the counter, his face full of smiles, busily attending to his business. He glanced at Li Sandie and his smile immediately faded, and he put on a cold face and said:

"Li Sandie, your wine bill must be paid today no matter what. It's not that I'm not being friendly, you know, the Mid-Autumn Festival is right around the corner - I also have to pay my wine bill to the people above." He ignored him and turned his head to welcome other customers.

This made Li Sandie embarrassed to step inside. At the same time, looking at Xing's boss's cold face, he felt a little unconvinced in his stomach. "Hmm, I'll give it to you in a while." He walked to the pier by the creek in a huff.

The pier was quiet and calm, without a single cargo ship. The reddish river water reflected the hot, dazzling sunlight, rippling with a myriad of golden waves, meandering and flowing peacefully.

The scorching sun had already moved overhead, making his head feel as if he were wearing a pot of blazing flames. "The Mid-Autumn Festival is in two days, why haven't the cargo ships come yet"? Looking at the empty river center, he couldn't help but feel anxious. So, he remembered the words his friend had said to him before: "Li Sandie, it would be more appropriate for you to find a business shop to work as a clerk." At that time, when he heard these words from his friend, a few points of pride would always appear in his heart, and he would reply with a smile, "I don't have any family burdens, I don't need to send letters home every month. This kind of life feels free, better, and happier! ...When I'm happy, I'll sell a few more jin of strength, when I'm unhappy, I'll take a nap all day, and I won't get anyone's anger or "Mang Ge" (restrictions). ..." At that time, he was so proud and admired by others.

Li Sandie knew that business was hopeless. At the same time, his stomach began to rumble again. So, he stretched a little, picked up his bamboo pole, and dragged his heavy footsteps back home.

Several hours of gazing at the riverbank had made him feel particularly tired in body and mind. As soon as he lay down on the floor, he fell fast asleep.

"Li Sandie, are you sleeping well? - My boss wants you to pay your wine bill"! Xing Ji Wine Shop's clerk woke him up.

"Damn it! There are still two days until the festival - I'm not going to run away from you."

Now, paying Xing's boss's wine bill was no longer on Li Sandie's mind. What was on his mind was: "It would be deadly if I don't have wine to drink for three days"!

The Bay in Early Winter 187

— Xin Ye

In the morning, the pale yellow sun spread flat on the sloping sandy beach. The wind of early winter, however, swam in the air, with a few withered leaves, like small gudgeons in muddy water, having nowhere to hide, and finally being knocked down. Only the catbrier bushes on the stone embankment still held up their needle-sharp green leaves, stubbornly squatting there. Occasionally, a gust of sea breeze would run over and pull at them, but they would merely shake their heads and remain quietly seated as before.

Along the beach, a row of not very neat fishing boats crowded together, about thirteen or fourteen of them. Each boat had three masts erected, and on the tip of each mast hung a large fishing net, forming a triangle that drooped below, like a row of large banners, fluttering in the sea breeze, which was quite a sight to behold.

On the stern of each of these fishing boats, breakfast was being cooked. Wisps of white smoke rose from under the tarpaulin, scattering into the air, allowing it to mix with the morning mist over the sea. The men were wiping away the heavy frost from the flat bases and gangways with damp mops, while some children jumped onto the beach to pick up seashells and pebbles.

Uncle Dasheng was on the bow of the boat, mending a broken fishing net under the sun. He stitched it together stitch by stitch, revealing a layer of undisguised melancholy and gloom on his dark and wrinkled face. Two streams of clear snot crawled out of his nostrils like green snakes, stretching towards his mouth. He wore only an old padded jacket with the cotton wadding already squeezed out of the holes. Under the sun, his two dry hands still trembled while holding a bamboo shuttle. However, that broken fishing net was as old and useless as he was himself. After mending one hole on the east side, another one appeared on the west side, and the net line was already brittle, so that with just a slight pull, it would tear into another hole. Yet he still had to rely on that broken net for a living, just as Dasheng's family of five had to rely on him, and he was unwilling to let go.

"This net is truly useless," he said, pushing it from his lap onto the flat base. Then, he pulled up another section and said, flipping it over, "I should have made a new one long ago, but... making a new one would cost more than ten dollars, and more than ten dollars is not easy to come by in this situation!"

Indeed, in recent years, he had been so weighed down by life that he could barely breathe. Business was bad, the burden of feeding his family was heavy, and there was often panic about meals. Where would he find the money to make a new net or add hooks? Even that old fishing boat had not been ashore for repairs or painting in more than ten years.

"Dad, it's time to eat!" While he was holding the broken net, lost in thought, his second son, Sanmao, called him for breakfast. Dasheng tightly rolled up the broken net, tossed it beside the rudder, lowered his head, and crawled into the tarpaulin tent.

"Today is a southeasterly wind. If the wind doesn't change this afternoon, it will definitely change tomorrow," Dasheng said after eating breakfast, wiping his mouth and standing on the bow to look at the sea. He saw that the damp mist was gradually receding, and the seashore had become much brighter. However, the muddy southeasterly wind continued to blow, dimming the sun's light.

"Dahuo, eat quickly. Let's go to the East Sea shallows early and set up the weirs," he said to his eldest son as he rolled up the tarpaulin.

"Are we going to pull them up after only a few days of setting them?"

"Yes, I think it's better to pull them up, to save them from being washed away by the waves in a strong wind!" His wife echoed in agreement.

More than a dozen fishing boats along the seashore had all rolled up their tarpaulins, tidied up their awning foot ropes, and sailed out onto the sea in succession. The iron anchors that had been submerged in the water were now all hoisted onto the bow of each boat.

In the afternoon, the bay was quiet and still, with not a single boat to be seen. Except for the surging of the waves and a few seabirds hopping on the sandy beach, the surroundings were left with only a boundless desolation!

The sky still wore a melancholic face, never showing a smile from morning until dusk. And the fishing boats had not yet returned.

Broadcasting

Boatman's Song

The Yangtze River flows eastward, slowly, slowly. Large and small boats travel east and west, upstream and downstream. Back and forth, the river flows long, back and forth, for ages. The morning sun shines, the river waves gleam. In the deep night, the bright moon reflects on the sandbar. Silly poets praise the boatman's joy, but who knows the boatman's sorrow!

The boatman's life relies on drifting, drifting, drifting. Eastward and westward, without stopping, with the current and against the current. Busy times mean no rest from the heat, idle times mean suffering from hunger. Paying taxes and dues, no money means committing a crime. The whole family's life is entrusted to the boat. Sometimes encountering fierce storms, the entire family perishes at once!

Storytelling 190

Xia Hesheng's Three Smiles

Dunben (800) 7:00 PM to 8:00 PM

Opening Chapter Pearl Tower "Falling Snow"

Dense clouds brew snow, snow condenses into ice, a sick Fang Qing is exhausted. He feels the mountain pass opening with the dawn, forgetting that the world has dusk. Heaven, with a cruel heart, blocks the mountain traveler. The piercing cold and sudden illness strike him, calling me, how can I walk when the snow beats and the wind blows? Seeing the lone goose following the lone traveler, fearing that it is not a traveler but a broken soul. Braving wind and frost, what is the meaning? Is it perhaps that Xiao Zheng is like me, seeking relatives far away? The winding path is hard to recognize, the road is rugged, and the lion's roar is frightening. The land is rugged and the sky is dark, even more pitiful that I am all alone. Moreover, where can I find an inn in a hurry? Wind gusts, snow falls, the mud is slippery, the night is deep, unable to distinguish the third watch from the fourth. Shredding and kneading cotton, the sky refuses to clear. Tonight, where can I stay? One step, one tear, one heartbreak. On the poor road, waving tears of longing for home, a band of mice from Bangxiao truly sees, and fake orangutans team up to overturn the traveler's bag.

Xing Ruiting's Hairpin Phoenix

Huiling (1380) 9:00 PM to 10:00 PM

Opening Chapter "Blood Splatters the Buddha Hall"

Orange and green in the small spring day, in the Buddhist Temple, let's talk about Buddhism, Sheng Gong's wonderful words, with flower tongue, believers listen respectfully, silently, Jian Qiao with the crowd sits, but see that, the killer of her father is also in the seat, suddenly, pear blossom face with frost, willow leaf eyebrows with anger, reaching into the bag to take the weapon for killing the enemy, knowing, that it is not on her body, she is, hiring a car reading speed going home, taking the heavy line before entering the seat, fortunately, the target is sitting still, the distance is only a foot away, years of investigation is not easy, the time has come, how can it be delayed, she is, using her silver teeth to bite and raise the weaver's hand, triggering the firing pin to open fire, only to see, where the gun fire sounds, the enemy is falling, blood is flying, his life is lost, thinking he is, for many years living in Jinmen, converting to my Buddha, before the Buddha, knowing, that he is still doomed to die, truly, the consequences are pre-ordained, and who is it, when he fell, not to be looked back at, Jian Qiao, is, constantly calling out, don't be afraid, reach into my chest, take out the printed material, say calmly to the crowd, shocking you, deeply guilty, I hope you forgive me, Jian Qiao, is, ten years of hatred is restored today, originally seeking death not immortality, calmly surrendering the weapon to the court, the attitude is calm not begging for pity, saying that the boudoir is full of talent, Jian Qiao's filial piety is combined, really talented in the boudoir.

Yi Hua Magazine 195

"Hero of the Hour" has been released in Jincheng, and this film is extremely successful. It can be called the unprecedented success of domestic sound films, especially the reality of the subject matter and the tragedy of the performance, which are most touching.

The photographer for "Wedding Night" is Wang Chunniao. Zhuang Jun is young, and "Wedding Night" is his virgin work, but the results are excellent. Whether it is the angle of the lens, the framing of the picture, or the combination of light, they all have special achievements.

"Triumph Song" has been completed, and Bu Wancang has great confidence. The Yi Hua authorities also attach great importance to it.

Fang Peilin's "Incarnation Girl" will start work around the 20th, and Xu Su's virgin film will also begin.

There are two newcomers in "Wedding Night," one is Lin Ling, who plays the writer's wife in the play. One is Zhang Li, who plays the playboy in the play. Both have wonderful performances, and their expressions and actions are both sophisticated and beautiful.

Several copies of "Hero of the Hour" have been sold, and telegrams from theaters all over the country requesting to rent and screen "Hero of the Hour" are also increasing daily. Even in the same place, two or three theaters are competing for the first-run screening rights. This shows the nationwide attention and desire for "Hero of the Hour."
